< Review>
I've been coming here for about a year and a half now and I love this place. I've never been treated so well at a nail salon. They are friendly, welcoming, and accommodating.

I go to Tim every two weeks for a fill on my acrylic nails and once a month I get a pedicure with any of the talented pedicurists.

Tim is friendly, a great nail tech, and extremely helpful to a indecisive person like me! He helps me pick a wonderful style every time--he suggests new colors and designs and gets my skinny square shape right every time! I like my nails to look very natural and he always makes sure I leave the shop with clean, natural looking nails.

Show him any style on your phone and he'll let you know if he can sufficiently give you that look. He is real about what can be done and upfront about the pricing.

Tim treats his regulars and new clients well! He's busy, so make sure to make an appointment if you'd like to see him!< /Review>

< review>
-BEDROOM:   Overpriced.   We had a 'deluxe double' bedroom which I thought was more roomy than it was. ...    It was one room, No fan in bathroom, but rooms were really warm in a good way.     Great beds,  great comforters.    Nice lounge chair and desk with two chairs.   Nice touch with the robes.
- PEOPLE WITH ANIMALS:  We  brought our dog and were only charged 75$ for 3 nights.   We were not charged 75$ per night per dog like the website said.      There is not a limit of 5 dogs per day total at the lodge, like the website says,   and I counted way more than 5.     All guests with dogs seemed to be housed in one row,  on the first floor,  rooms 177 to 191,  and the back yard area was grass with too much doggie doodoo that guests weren't picking up.     LOVED the doggie doodoo bags,   the dog bed,  dog toys and water bowl.    They were very welcoming to our dog and that was great!!
-VIEW:  The lodge is renovating the pool and the back side,  and our view was a green fence with dirt and tractors.    For the price,  I was very disappointed in the view out of our back sliding glass window and thought the lodge should have said something to us, or reduced the price.      There was no tractor construction while we were there, no noise,  but,  still the view was horrible.
-HAD TO WALK OUTSIDE LODGE TO GET TO ROOM -- I thought it was strange that we had to walk outside the lodge to get to our room...  You'd think that with a hotel in Yosemite,  you could walk inside or outside to get to the main lodge area/restaurants...
-NICE STAFF  --   great staff.
-VALET:    VALET IS free,  but warning,  we used it once, called 1/2 hour in advance and when we went out,  it wasn't there....    so we self parked and didnt use valet the rest of the day.
-FOOD:    the food was nothing to write home about.
-CHRISTMAS BUFFET:   really nice.     great staff,   very good food, but again,  pretty average.
-ACTIVITIES:   we went ice skating in Yosemite,   and did ROCK CLIMBING at the lodge,..    super fun.< /review>

<Rate>1</Rate><text>I strongly believe that all of this was well planned, it makes perfect sense and is pretty smart if you think about it, Colonial Moving & Storage if a Broker so what they do is cold call you using information they obtain from U-Haul, Penske & Budget Rentals (we know this because those were the 1st three we called before talking with Colonial. So, they get your info, make contact and give you a price significantly lower than quoted by the moving companies. They then have you pay a deposit then sell you contract to another company, obviously they are all working together and know this. Calstate Moving & Storage, Hermes Moving and Storage& Cross-Country Movers in our case. Calstate then controls the contract and uses its other businesses as sort of buffers, if the other businesses get in trouble, fines or complained on they can always just Do Business As (DBA) with a new name. Now instead of having to complain on one company in one state your dealing with 4 (or more) companies in 2 different states.  Now it becomes difficult to file a complaint of a law suit.
Here is what we have done and are doing.

We contacted the Better Business Bureau who gave us an amazing amount of information and insight. We filed a complaint with them on Calstate Moving & Storage, Hermes Moving and Storage & Colonial Moving & Storage. We contacted & filed a complaint with the Department of Transportation in California, New Mexico & Florida. I contacted & filed a complaint with the Federal Department of Transportation and the Federal Motor Carrier Safety Administration. We contacted and filed a complaint with the California Public Utilities Commission, the California Whistleblowers Association and the California State Attorney Generals Office. We contacted and filed a complaint with the Federal Trade Commission (who put our names on a list for a class action law suit) and Immigration Customs Enforcement. Every where we called to complain were very helpful and gave us insight into contacting another agency that might be able to help. We are also in the process of posting complaints to My Moving Reviews, BBB, Yelp, Google & Yahoo Reviews so that no on else ever gets scammed like us.

6033 Barton Ave. Los Angeles, CA 90038

Colonial Moving & Storage ‚Äì (Steve Roth ‚Äì Sales Rep., Tammy ‚Äì Accounting, Amanda ‚Äì Operations Manager, Sarah Drumand ‚Äì Unknown, Jessica McBride ‚Äì Unknown)

<userid>114677102471032013705</userid>< Text>
Visited this place with my husband and son on a Friday night. The place wasn't that crowded, there were two other families seated. I should add that we went around 7:45 and I didn't realize the place closed at 8:30. We ordered a calamari appetizer and were served warm bread while waiting for our food to arrive. The bread was so good, I could have had a whole basket of that for dinner. It had a little crunch to it but was super soft and warm inside. Calamari was good as well. We ordered the "deep dish" pizza as our main entree. I understood that the deep dish took a little longer than a normal pizza would which was totally fine. It arrived and I was not as satisfied as I thought I would be. The crust on the bottom was pretty thin and it was mainly just a big glob of cheese, like, too much cheese. It became overbearing to the point it seemed as though we were just eating bug globs of cheese, not much filling in between that. I would visit again but probably steer away from the deep dish pizza.<//Text>

<rating>2<//rating>< Review>
The good part of Rocklin Smiles is the pleasant and friendly atmosphere inside the building. Everyone is going out of their way to make you feel comfortable. The two stars however are an evaluation prompted by the actual work and its consequences. I went in just for a checkup with no pain or issues.  Dr Maasri stated that she detected a cavity and that the best solution would be a crown. We proceeded with the procedure but I was somewhat uneasy by the process; most of the actual crown work was done by an assistant (technician) and the post bite adjustment took maybe 5 minutes.  Dr. Maasri told me that I could come back for any issue. The pain over the next days was pretty substantial and grew to chronic pain into my lower and upper jaw reaching my cheekbone. When I started waking up at nights, I made a new appointment. During the second appointment new adjustment to my bite were done but again pain drove me to take ibuprofen for pain reduction and possible inflammation. After my third visit the bite was finally corrected as it should be and now I am pain free.
Again, the office is trying to be super friendly but the actual dentist work seems to be rushed in completion. My days and nights of pain could have been prevented by an extra 15-30 minutes of bite correction; it seems the dentist did not have the needed experience to identify and complete the bite correction properly.< /Review>

< text>
I just wanted to inform fellow customers of their own safety and health. I came here a few days ago to grab a dozen cupcakes for my Mother‚Äôs birthday. As I was waiting in line there were two people in front of me without a mask. I tried to keep a distance away from them and hoped that the employees would ask them to wear a mask. By law, everyone is required to wear a mask when entering businesses and even in general. However, the employee proceeded to serve them and continued to have a small conversation with the customers about the flavors they offered. By then, I was furious at how the store was not taking correct precautions, especially when we are in a pandemic. With cases rising, I wanted to support local small businesses as I love their key lime pie cupcakes and their salted caramel cupcakes. However, I do not think I will be coming back here for a while. The employee also used the same gloves to wipe down a counter with a dirty towel, and proceeded to serve another customer. Lastly, I also noticed a person coming from out back to talk to their employee without a mask on. (Possibly a manager)? The environment itself at this store seems to be hazardous, not only to the customers, but possibly to their employees as well. As a nurse, I do not accept this type of carelessness in the food industry during a pandemic.<//text>

I really went to Swan Market to grab a savory lunch meal, but that's the  best part about a market - there are endless, tempting food options!  Of course being the dessert lover that I am, I initially was eyeing the chocolate chip cookies at Cosecho.  Then all of a sudden my homegirl said, "Oh you're looking in the wrong direction if you want that good good!" And I turned my attention to my beloved Cupcakin' Bake Shop!

What do I love about Cupcakin' you ask?
-Offers a nice assortment of cupcake flavors as well as sizes (get a regular size & a mini so you can try 2 flavors and not feel like your overdoing it!)
-The bright d√©cor is very inviting
-The staff is super friendly
-The cupcakes are DELICIOUS (icing is sweet, cake is moist, and it is everything your taste buds need)!

The Chocolate Salted Caramel was divine and the surprise of the salt at the bottom of the cupcake...oooh wee!  The Red Velvet delivered as well.  Cupcakes are priced well too - minis are $1.95 & regular size are $3.75.

This place prides itself on being local (owner is an Oakland native), artisan, and it is a black owned business.  And if you're in the BeyHive, you'll be elated because Beyonc√© music was in heavy rotation.

< review>
So here is the thing. I have to be blatantly honest. This bakery has a case full of what "appear" to be beautifully baked goods, in a cute shop, in charming downtown Claremont. So what's the problem?  Looks are very deceiving. The pastries were so beautiful we couldn't wait to get home and brew a cup of coffee and try each one.  To our massive disappointment, none were good. We mean, none.  At best, the almond croissant gets 3 of 5. I am still baffled at how pretty the baked goods compared to tasting so bland.  A total of 5 adult and teen tasters, who couldn't approve of even one pastry.

The fruit tart crust to custard ratio must be improved. Frankly, it was like eating a thick piece of crust with a few pieces of fresh fruit. Just meh.

The fruit, cheese, and almond Danish pictured are just blah....  and we mean blah...

We also purchased a loaf of sourdough bread (not pictured), that was a bit stale and also lacked in flavor. $35 wasted as we threw out the baked goods.

By far, we much rather go to Some Crust Bakery.  In a blind taste test, Creme Bakery would lose to Ralph's bakery.  Too bad üëé.< /review>

< Review>

< Text>
This has become our go to Ramen place. The food is great. The service is fast and friendly. The Ramen is of course the main event - tasty, you can make it spicy for a buck, customized toppings, choice of broth - piping hot! But the appetizer list is a killer - i almost think of skipping the Ramen - chicken, edamame, roasted pork, scallops - the bomb.
Also the yelp wait-list is the only way to go. Otherwise you will get stuck standing out and getting hungry and angry.

Go!</Text>

Great takeout during COVID. Was really craving ramen and this was one of the closest places that offered takeout. < review>
If you're craving some Ramen as well as other creative and delicious Japanese cuisines,  then "Orenchi Ramen" on Broadway in Redwood City is your 'Go-To' Spot. Trendy crowd,  busy atmosphere and professional service from a friendly staff is the best way to describe this resto. Due to is popularity, there was about a 15 minute wait to be seated. But it was worth it.  We hung out inside where it was warm and cozy.. The dining area was filled with a plethora of appetizing aromas. Decent prices too.  Enjoy!<//review>

< text>
Wait is long during peak times of the day. Karaage is juicy. Ramen noodles are delicious, toppings are conservative. Spicy costs extra. Environment is cozy. Staff is friendly. Location is across from the  Caltrain station. Definitely a great place to eat in Redwood City. Just make sure you have some time to wait.< /text>

< Text>
My friend and I choose this spot out of convenience for the both of us. I had to drive down from SF after flying in from LA and he drove up from SJ and Redwood Citt was the midpoint we choose. We cane here on a Saturday night around 6 and there was some wait to it but it wasn't too long of a wait. As we were led to our table, the server just handed us the menu and away we searched for our meal. We decided on their Orenchi ramen, since it's in their name so it had to be good. Turns out, the broth is full of flavor but nothing really wowed me. I honestly believe ramen in LA tastes better than this place like Shinshengumi or even Daikokuya. The ramen we ordered doesn't have a great presentation when given at the table. Everything is always about presentation, especially when it comes to food.

Next in this review are their two appetizers we ordered; shishito peppers and beer battered onion rings. The peppers were lacking in flavor but some of them had a great kick. Onion rings were probably my favorite at this ramen shop. Nicely fried and hot all around. What threw me off was that they served it with a piece of shishito pepper on top. Nonetheless, I enjoyed every bite.</Text>

<rating>1<//rating>< text>
I've been to bad restaurants and wonder why they got good ratings, but Orenchi is still a big surprise for me.
Seeing the great reviews on Google Map and Yelp, I decided to come here for lunch. Waiting was fine, but my foods came out horrifying.
Despite my Karamiso ramen has a layer of pork fat floating on the broth, it still barely has any flavor but saltiness. The Chasiu was just a thin piece of bland boiled pork.
The onion rings came out as some home cook tried to make onion rings from scratch for the first time and miserably failed. It was soggy and soaked with oil, and it dripped oil all over the table.
Like most ramen places, there's basically no service.
I really couldn't understand how did they make it so far with several locations. This is the worst ramen place I have tried so far in the bay area, no one of.</text>

<review>The last-last time I went to Orenchi, I thought it was okay but not really that good or impressive. *This* time, however, struck a different tune. Right from the get-go, my impression (first impression for this location, anyway) was positive. While looking for parking, I was able to use the Yelp app to add my name to the waiting list. Then upon arriving, the remaining wait was only a few minutes despite how busy it was (I don't think the other people waiting seemed very happy about it though, since it looked like I skipped the line lol); we were seated at the bar. My bf and I shared the karaage chicken which seemed like a huge portion, even for sharing. Then we both (separately) ordered one of the ramens that were on special. Everything was delicious, and seemed even better by the fact that we had been driving around for a while looking for a place to eat before finding this one on the app. I'm glad I gave Orenchi another go since I was def impressed ;)<//review>< Pics>

We're getting direct from Japanese restaurants and this has raised the standard for everyone. Orenchi is still the touchstone, but the competition is fierce now. < Review>
The ramen is absolutely delicious. The *only* detail I would have liked differently is that I prefer to have the egg with a gooey yolk. They also have a good, albeit slight sweet, sake on tap and a good selection of non-ramen dishes.

The venue is also nicely styled to feel like a street-side ramen bar. While it can be a bit crowded, and it seems to fill up fast, it doesn't feel like the space is overfilled.

The prices are also sightly more expensive than I'd expect, but the food is very well prepared, and considering how quickly I received it, I'm very happy with my experience.</Review>

< Review>
Ramen was disappointing, despite being so busy.
This place always seems to be packed with people. But after eating here I'm not sure why. We got edamame and two of the three ramens dishes on the regular menu. It's hard to mess up edamame so that was fine. The ramen though was downright disappointing. It wasn't horrible, just lacked any depth of flavor. The pork was thin and flavorless, I even got extra meat and it wasn't nearly enough. The broths were only okay...the broth should be the main attraction! They don't even provide any condiments to add (bean sprouts, Sriracha, soy, other sauces, etc.). Very underwhelming experience after all the hype.</Review>

<time>1526133340355< /time><Rate>4< /Rate><Text>For fans of the original location in Santa Clara, Orenchi is Redwood City is a welcome and much needed ramen option on the Peninsula. While SF has a plethora of options (Mensho, Marufuke, Ippudo, Orenchi Beyond), the Peninsula has largely been only Santa Ramen and its outposts Ramen Dojo and Parlour that are all mentioned less frequently with greater competition coming from Japan.

Orenchi is often acknowledged as one of the best, if not the best ramen shops in the South Bay, mainly for their signature tonkotsu broth, in house made thick noodles, and perfect ramen eggs.

Lines are nowhere as long as the Santa Clara outpost but Redwood City is an upcoming area and enough young people and tech workers  (Box is nearby) are such that the sign up list had 10 people before even opening.

Thankfully, food service is fairly efficient and appetizers and ramen comes out promptly. We enjoyed the Karaage (signature item given Sumika background), the spicy fries with wasabi, and the Ikura Gohan.  Tip: prepare for a wait, sample the appetizers, and enjoy a great bowl of ramen in the Peninsula.</Text><pictures>None<//pictures>< resp>

<time>1517589686053< /time><rate>4<//rate><Text>No line at Orenchi? Pinch me please!

We showed up about 10 minutes before the dinner soft opening on February 1st and was shocked to have no wait.

The service was great. The staff was full of excitement on opening day, and our food came out extra fast and steaming hot.

I liked the chicken karaage better than in Sunnyvale - medium-thick breading, extra crispy, and juicy! The pieces were very large too.

They didn't have the awesome Ore No Tan Tan Men (miso, sesame) available yet, so we got the Orenchi Ramen (tonkotsu) and the Shoyu Ramen (soy sauce).

I loved the springy, al dente noodles! The Shoyu Ramen had straighter, thinner noodles which I slightly preferred. I also liked that the soy sauce broth wasn't too salty, and it had good depth of flavor.

The tonkotsu broth here was a bit light for my taste, but the chili and garlic paste amped it up. Don‚Äôt miss out on that garlic paste! It added nice depth without being too harsh.

I thought the chashu pork was pretty average and thin, but the broth and noodles were great on both bowls.

Hitachino Nest on tap was perfect to wash it all down.

Definitely a welcome addition to the ramen desert here! I'll be a regular.< /Text><Pics>None<//Pics>< resp>
None< /resp>
<gmapID>0x808fa24d5ce2e733:0xb91e4f7c4e66cb23<//gmapID></record></dataset><record>
<userid>103465236820333032452</userid>< user_name>
Gill Tan</user_name>
<Time>1519632569084< /Time>< Rate>
5< /Rate>
< review>
I've been to Dojo, Parlor, Santa, etc, but I like Orenchi the best. Their tonkotsu ramen with spicy miso is to die for.

The ramen is always served piping hot, noodles perfectly al dente, eggs soft boiled with runny yolk, chashu lightly roasted so it's tender and melts in your mouth, and broth kotteri (with emulsi pork fat) so that it's extra rich and creamy. The spicy miso gives it just the right kick to make it the perfect bowl, so it's definitely worth the wait.

I've tried most of the appetizers, and you can't go wrong with any of them. But the ones that stood out the most to me were the nankotsu karage (fried chicken cartilage with sweet glaze), spicy fries (served with wasabi aeoli *amazing*), and chashu gohan (marinated pork belly over rice). If you get the chance, try the hitachino on tap, you won't regret it.

This is a great place to go to grab drinks and food with your friends. It's always bustling and they always have good music playing. It's a much needed establishment in the ramen desert that is this part of the peninsula. Make sure to get there early to put your name down on the wait list, or get their like 45 minutes before closing if you want to avoid the wait.< /review>
